We could have continued (this is not a bad place), but we made a decision to
backtrack in these situations, so let's backtrack, redo the first 640 steps and
then try to continue differently.

```
julia> serialize("cf-s2-100-parameters-opt.ser", opt)

julia> serialize("cf-s2-100-parameters-matrix.ser", trainable["network_matrix"])
```

Now we have a nice 100 parameter model with a nasty property that if one
cuts the smallest weight the performance is completely destroyed.

A possible TODO item: to investigate the structure of this model.

**Another important note: there are some discrepancies between the first 640 steps
of the runs; not too much, so there is nice continuity here (robustness with respect
to noise), but it is worrying that reproducibility is less than perfect in this case.
TODO: this really needs to be investigated and understood.**

We'll try to continue training this with a hope that it will move to
the state when cutting parameters is OK. Indeed, it turnes out that it's
enough to do a hundred non-sparsifying steps, and we are back in the situation
when we can do 1 sparsification per 20 steps:


This 85-parameter model is likely to have an unfortunate property to deteriorate
sharply when the lowest weight is cut. We'll try again to push it past that state.

So, we are going to redo this and obtain an 82-parameter model
(all this needs to be automated).

Restart Julia and do that; we obtain an 82-parameter model, which trains nicely,
but even after 100 steps one cannot cut the smallest element without catastrophic
deterioration (we need to instrument this better, so that we can note the indices
of those elements and perhaps to mark them "un-deletable" for some period of time.

```
julia> serialize("cf-s2-82-parameters-improved-2-matrix.ser", trainable["network_matrix"])
```

We want to know **the value and the indices** of the weight
we are about to eliminate. (If something sits on some sort of
critical path, then it might even be relatively small and still
crucial, so knowing the indices is important.)

```julia
function min_ind_dict(x::Dict{String, Dict{String, Dict{String, Dict{String, Float32}}}})
    min_v = 1.0f8
    indices = ("not found", "not found", "not found", "not found")
    for i in keys(x)
        for j in keys(x[i])
            for m in keys(x[i][j])
                for n in keys(x[i][j][m])
                    v = x[i][j][m][n]
                    if abs(v) < min_v
                        min_v = abs(v)
                        indices = (i, j, m, n)
                    end
    end end end end
	(min_v, indices)
end
```

Let's add this to our codebase.

```

```

What we see is that

```
julia> min_ind_dict(trainable["network_matrix"])
(0.0040694075f0, ("accum-2-1", "dict-2", "accum-1-2", "dict"))
```

is the sign of trouble; we need to avoid cutting this element off.

As we'll see below, this element is also the culprit for the problem
observed at 67 parameters.

For now let's keep track of this manually:

```

```

As we see, this worked reasonably well, although the end of preregularization loss
improvement (and even some degradation in that parameter) is a concern.

Now, with this model, we know that cutting this element is probably a very bad idea.

So we'll do a bit of non-sparsifying training to get rid of this element being
the smallest.
